<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="removing-a-mask">Removing a mask<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#removing-a-mask" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Untie the bottom, then top tie</li>
<li>Remove from face</li>
<li>Discard</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="limitation-of-ppe">Limitation of PPE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#limitation-of-ppe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>They don't remove the contaminants</li>
<li>Protection given by PPE is limited (i.e. efficacy and time factor must be considered)</li>
<li>PPE often cause high extra physical load</li>
<li>Sometimes it is difficult to get proper fit due to different anatomical features of the wearer</li>
<li>They may cause aesthetic problem</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="theatre-attire">Theatre attire<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theatre-attire" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The purpose of theatre attire is to provide a barrier that protects the patient from micro-organisms, which are shed into the environment from the skin and hair of theatre personnel, and to protect the outside environment from theatre contaminants.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; All personnel entering restricted areas of the operating department wear designated theatre attire, thus decreasing the potential for wound infections in surgical patients.</p>
<p>&gt; It is essential that all staff receive instruction as to the correct manner of dressing within the operating department, including information about the need for strict personal hygiene, good health and the implications of these to patient care.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Theatre attire is also a means of identifying theatre personnel.</li>
<li>Theatre attire is designed to minimise the transfer of micro-organisms from the mucous membranes, skin and hair of the surgical team to the patient.</li>
<li>It also provides the surgical team with some protection from the patient.</li>
<li>When selecting theatre clothing (reusable or single-use), it is important to consider the quality of material in relation to the dissemination of airborne bacteria and bacterial strike-through. All personnel who enter the restricted area of the theatre suite should don the attire intended for use within the surgical environment.</li>
<li>Sufficient supplies of theatre clothing should be provided daily and clean theatre clothing should be protected from possible contamination during transfer and storage.</li>
<li>Theatre attire should consist of a two-piece trouser suit. It should also be:</li>
<li>made of a close-knit material with antistatic properties</li>
<li>resistant to bacterial strike-through</li>
<li>flame resistant</li>
<li>lint-free, as lint(tiny fibres of fabric that are shed from the edges of clothes) can increase the number of airborne particulates</li>
<li>coloured to reduce glare</li>
<li>cool and comfortable with maximum skin covering</li>
<li>professional in appearance</li>
<li>Provided freshly laundered and in good condition</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
25
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Hands should be washed before and after donning theatre attire.</li>
<li>Theatre attire should be removed when it becomes wet or soiled, and placed into containers specially designed for contaminated laundry, to reduce the potential for cross-contamination.</li>
<li>Theatre attire should be changed following environmental cleaning of the operating theatre and before the commencement of a new operating list.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="headwear">Headwear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#headwear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>All head and facial hair should be covered completely by a head cover/cap - surgical site infections have been traced to organisms isolated from the hair and scalp.</li>
<li>Disposable headwear is preferable, however cloth hats are permissible if laundered and inspected for holes/imperfections in an approved facility.</li>
<li>Headwear should be donned prior to donning the scrub suit.</li>
<li>This eliminates the possibility of hair or dandruff being shed onto scrub clothing.</li>
<li>Headwear should be changed daily, unless it becomes soiled, when it should be changed immediately.</li>
<li>Headwear should always be worn in laminar flow theatres during prosthetic implant operations (ICNA 2002).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="jewellery">Jewellery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#jewellery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Jewellery should be removed as it has been shown to increase surface bacterial counts when left in situ.</li>
<li>Finger nails should be clean, short and free from nail varnish.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Short nails are less likely to puncture gloves and therefore reduce the risk of harming the patient through transfer.</li>
<li>False finger nails, including acrylic or gel-coated nails should not be worn.</li>
<li>These have been shown to harbour micro-organisms such as fungi and Gram-negative bacteria even after hand washing; they can also inhibit hand washing (Hedderwick et al 2000, McNeil et al 2000, NICE 2008).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="masks">Masks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#masks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The rationale for wearing masks in a surgical setting is to contain the micro-organisms expelled from the mouth and nose.</li>
<li>They also protect the wearer from potential splashes of body fluids and blood.</li>
<li>Masks may offer some protection from inhalation of surgical smoke and laser plume. Filtration levels vary according to manufacturers specification and masks should be selected according to the level of protection required, E.g exposure to mycobacterium tuberculosis. The wearing of masks in theatre is questionable, except during prosthetic implant operation (Hospital Infection Society 2002).</li>
<li>Facilities should develop their own policies and guidelines in relation to the wearing of masks.</li>
<li>Protective face shields should be worn whenever activities could place personnel at risk of splashes or aerosol contamination.</li>
<li>Occasionally filtration masks may be required when dealing with certain patients such as those with pulmonary tuberculosis.</li>
<li>Masks should cover the nose and mouth, fitting the contour of the face and should be tied securely. The user should avoid touching the mask once it is applied.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>A used mask should be handled by the tapes only.</li>
<li>Used masks should be discarded into an appropriate container for disposal after each case or if soiled.</li>
<li>Masks should not be left around the neck or put into pockets for future use. Hands should be washed following mask removal.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cover-gowns-laboratory-coats">Cover gowns/laboratory coats<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cover-gowns-laboratory-coats" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ideally, all theatre personnel should change into outdoor clothing before leaving the theatre environment; however AfPP recognises that this is not always feasible.</li>
<li>If theatre personnel are required to leave the theatre environment without changing, fully fastened and clean over jackets may be worn, as determined by the individual practice setting. However, if this is accepted and authorised practice, then there must be arrangements made to ensure that there is a sufficient supply of clean cover gowns available.</li>
<li>Theatre attire should be removed before leaving the theatre environment and placed into an appropriate container.</li>
<li>When leaving the clinical area, personnel should change into their outdoor clothes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nb">NB:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fresh, clean attire should be donned on return to theatre</li>
<li>Used theatre attire should not be stored in lockers for further use.</li>
<li>Theatre attire should not be worn outside the clinical area or in public places.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="footwear">Footwear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#footwear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Footwear in theatres should provide adequate protection and a risk assessment should be done to determine whether the type of footwear is suitable for decontamination.</li>
<li>The purpose of such footwear is to provide antistatic properties in accordance with WHO recommendations</li>
<li>Footwear that is not supplied by the employer may not meet all the necessary standards. Footwear should be well fitting, supportive and protective.</li>
<li>Shoes should provide protection from spillages and accidentally dropped equipment. Footwear worn in theatres should be for that use only and should be cleaned regularly (using appropriate PPE) to remove any contaminants.</li>
<li>The use of washer-disinfectors or autoclaves is preferable for the decontamination of footwear (ICNA 2002).</li>
<li>Auto-clavable footwear should therefore be available to personnel. It is each individual health</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laundering-of-theatre-attire">Laundering of theatre attire<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laundering-of-theatre-attire" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The home laundering of theatre attire is not recommended.</li>
<li>The rationale for laundering in an approved hospital facility is to prevent soiled clothing from spreading contaminants into the home environment and to ensure that laundering of clothing is in accordance with relevant standards (DH 1995, AfPP 2011).</li>
<li>Hospitals have approved laundry facilities or have contracts with laundry companies in which laundry processes are monitored and assessed and laundry can be handled in conjunction with standard precautions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="take-home-message-as-ppe-are-concerned">Take home message as PPE are concerned<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#take-home-message-as-ppe-are-concerned" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>In conclusion it is important to note that the material of PPE chosen must be able to withstand the specific hazard prevailing in a specific workplace</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ethical-legal-aspects-in-theatre-nursing">Ethical/Legal aspects in Theatre Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-legal-aspects-in-theatre-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Legal. The dictionary defines the word legal as 'required' or 'permitted by law'.</li>
<li>Therefore, when we talk of legal aspects in theatre nursing, we are referring to what the law requires us to do in the theatre before, during and after the operation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="important-considerations">Important considerations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#important-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Right to life/principle of justice</li>
<li>Respect of autonomy-respect to ones opinion</li>
<li>Principle of non-maleficence  do no harm (beneficence)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-encountered-legal-issues">Common encountered legal issues<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-encountered-legal-issues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Consent, Negligence, inadequate documentation, inexperience, clinical errors, confidentiality, patients security.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="consent">Consent:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#consent" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Consent must be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Legally valid e.g. given by a person above 18 years, of sound mind and voluntary not coerced</li>
<li>Administered by a competent doctor</li>
<li>Must be informed</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-negligence">1). Negligence:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-negligence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Clinician not providing adequate /reasonable information about risks of proposed treatment.</li>
<li>Inadequate documentation: improper and incomplete notes, lack of documentation.</li>
<li>Inexperience /inadequate experience/lack of experience: No clinician is an expert of everything, clinician should seek appropriate guide/supervision and refuse to proceed.</li>
<li>Clinical errors (not negligence) clinician need to be honest and apologetic for their mistakes, this is not admitting negligence. Patients accept apologies but not explanations.</li>
</ul>
<p>2). Confidentiality: This is another legal requirement.</p>
<ul>
<li>In the definition of legal, the term permitted by law implies that you can only carry out patient care within what the law permits you to do.</li>
<li>Therefore, the law gives the patient seeking medical, surgical and nursing care, rights under which they are to be managed.</li>
</ul>
<p>3). Security/Safety of the patient before, during and after operation is vested in the theatre team. By signing the consent form, the patient takes some responsibility for the whole loss of life or part of their body. However, this does not take away the responsibility of the theatre team to ensure the security of the patient's life during the operation.</p>
<p>4). Consent: It is on this basis that those below the legal age of adulthood (18 years in Kenya) are not legally bound to sign the consent form.</p>
<ul>
<li>It is signed by the parents/guardians on their behalf. In the same way, consent for the mentally ill is sought from their parents/guardians/relatives.</li>
<li>It is also important to note that consent for an operation should be obtained from the patient before they are pre-medicated, as pre-medication drugs have the potential of affecting their reasoning capacity, hence making consent signed not legally binding.</li>
<li>The legal aspect in theatre nursing involves the care of the patient from the time the patient is accepted in theatre, until they are handed over back to the ward.</li>
<li>For these reasons, the following procedure should be adhered to:</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>31</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Any patient going to theatre must be properly prepared preoperatively.
The patient must be well labelled (identification)
The patient must sign an informed consent, obtained by the surgeon.
The patient must be protected from any harm, falls or eventuality, during the stay in theatre.
Confidentiality must be observed regarding the patient.
Measures must be taken to ensure that the patient taken to theatre is the right one for the intended operation.
The items to be used for the operation must be counted and recorded before and after operation to prevent loss of swabs, tubes, blades, forceps, abdominal pacts and any instrument used.
Theatre nurses must know where the exits are, for use in case of an emergency.
Sockets in theatre should be covered during scrubbing to prevent risk of conducting currents. They should also be one meter or more above the floor level.
All electrical machines must be checked to ascertain optimum function before use on the patient.
Documentation/record keeping in theatre</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ethical-and-legal-aspects-of-peri-operative-nursing">Ethical and legal aspects of peri-operative nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-and-legal-aspects-of-peri-operative-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Perioperative nurses often find ethical decisions difficult to make, but necessary when caring for surgical patients in practice.</li>
<li>Perioperative nurses need to be able to recognize <strong>ethical dilemmas</strong> and take appropriate action as warranted.</li>
<li>They are responsible for nursing decisions that are not only clinically and technically sound but also morally appropriate and suitable for the specific problems of the</li>
</ul>
<p>32</p>
<p>particular patient being treated. The technical or medical aspects of nursing practice answer the question, What can be done for the patient?</p>
<ul>
<li>The moral component involves the patient's wishes and answers the question, What ought to be done for the patient?</li>
<li>The code of ethics expresses the moral commitment to uphold the goals, values and distinct ethical obligations of all nurses.</li>
</ul>
<p>An <strong>ethical dilemma</strong> involves the need to choose from among two or more morally acceptable options or between equally unacceptable courses of action, when one choice prevents selection of the other.</p>
<p><strong>NB</strong>: Nursing is practiced in a changing social context/world, so the code of ethics has become a dynamic document.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-perioperative-nursing-code">The perioperative nursing code<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-perioperative-nursing-code" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The code for perioperative nurses provide the framework in which perioperative nurses can make ethical decisions.</li>
<li>The code establishes a non-negotiable ethical standard for the nursing profession.</li>
<li>It demonstrates accountability and responsibility to the public, other members of the health care team and the profession overall.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bioethical-principles">BIOETHICAL PRINCIPLES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bioethical-principles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The term <strong>ethical</strong> refers to reasons individuals have for the decisions they make about how they ought to act.</li>
<li>The term <strong>moral</strong> overlaps the term ethical, but it is more aligned with an individual's personal beliefs and cultural values.</li>
<li>Underlying nurses' ethical actions are the principles of bioethics, which have a great deal of influence on perioperative nursing practices and these principles include the following:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Autonomy</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>33</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>That is an individual's self-determination, which is the principle that encompasses respect for others and allows individuals to make voluntary, uncoerced decisions about life situations</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Beneficence</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>This is the principle of doing good, benefiting, or acting in the best interests of the patient, health care providers should strive to do this for their patients</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Non-maleficence</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>This is the principle that directs health care providers to do no harm, it is often not enough to do good for a patient, but non-maleficence must be considered proportionally when health care decisions are being made</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Justice</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>This is the principle that states individuals should be treated according to what is fair or owed to them (i. e, patients expect to be treated fairly and to receive equal care despite of the colour, social status, religion etc)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Confidentiality / fidelity</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The principle refers to the keeping of promises, as patients expect health care providers will keep their promises to maintain the confidentiality and privacy of patient information</li>
</ul>
<ol start="6">
<li>Security/Safety</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>This refers to the safety of the patient before, during and after operation is vested in the theatre team. By signing the consent form, the patient takes some responsibility for the whole loss of life or part of their body. However, this does not take away the responsibility of the theatre team to ensure the security of the patient's life during the operation.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="7">
<li>Truthful/ veracity</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>This is the principle of truth telling, patients expect health care providers to be truthful about their care</li>
<li>Veracity is defined as being honest and telling the truth and is related to the principle of autonomy. It is the basis of the trust relationship established between a</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>patient and a health care provider. This allows patients to use their autonomy to make decisions in their own best interest.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Medical negligence :</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>In general, negligence involves a person's failure to exercise care in a way that a reasonable person would have done/exercised care in a/under similar situation/circumstance.</li>
<li>Medical negligence applies when a medical provider makes a mistake in treating patient and that mistake results in harm to the patient</li>
</ul>
<ol start="9">
<li>Medical malpractice:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Malpractice is a type of negligence that specifically relates to licensed professionals who fail to provide services that meet the required standard of care</li>
<li>It also mean the breach of the duty of care by a medical provider or medical facility.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="10">
<li>Consent:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>It is on this basis that those below the legal age of adulthood (18 years in Kenya) are not legally bound to sign the consent form.</li>
<li>It is signed by the parents/guardians on their behalf. In the same way, consent for the mentally ill is sought from their parents/guardians/relatives.</li>
<li>It is also important to note that consent for an operation should be obtained from the patient before they are pre-medicated, as pre-medication drugs have the potential of affecting their reasoning capacity, hence making consent signed not legally binding.</li>
</ul>
<p>These principles often come into conflict with the values of those involved in ethical decision making. It may be difficult for patients, nurses, and other health care providers to prioritize between principles because the context of each situation may vary.</p>
<p>Code of Ethics for Nurses with interpretive statements</p>
<p>Respect for people</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>35</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The nurse, in all professional relationships, practices with compassion and respect for the inherent dignity, worth and uniqueness of every individual, unrestricted by considerations of social or economic status, personal attributes, or the nature of health problems.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This provision clarifies that perioperative nurses should have respect for human dignity, especially in the context of their relationships with patients and taking into account the nature of patients' health problems.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nurses also should respect human dignity in their relationships with their colleagues and others in the health care setting. This provision also addresses the right of patients and nurses to self-determination. In terms of behavior, the overall concept expressed is respect for people.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supporting-patient-rights-and-choices">Supporting patient rights and choices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supporting-patient-rights-and-choices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nurses are obligated morally to respect the dignity and worth of individual patients.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nursing care must be provided in a manner that preserves and protects patient autonomy and human rights. Nurses have an obligation to be knowledgeable about the moral and legal rights of their patients and to protect and support those rights. Health care does not occur in a vacuum, so perioperative nurses must take into account both individual rights and interdependence in decision making.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>By doing so, nurses can recognize situations in which individual rights to self-determination in health care temporarily should be overridden to preserve the life of the human community. E.g., during a bioterrorism attack, victims infected with transmissible organisms (E.g., small pox) require infection control measures to prevent transmission to others. These infection control measures may require isolation, resulting in restricting a patient's right to freedom of movement to protect others.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nurses preserve and protect their patients' autonomy, dignity, and human rights with specific nursing interventions, including supporting a patient's</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>participation in decision making, confirming informed consent and implementing facility advance directive policies.</p>
<ul>
<li>Perioperative nurses explain procedures and the operating room environment before initiating actions and they respect patients' wishes in regard to advance directives and end-of-life choices.</li>
<li>Perioperative nurses help patients make choices within their scope of care as applicable. They also provide patients with honest and accurate answers to their questions, especially related to perioperative teaching, and formulate ethical decisions with help from available resources (eg, ethics committee, counselors, ethicists).</li>
<li>Patients have the right to self-determination (ie, the ability to decide for oneself what course of action will be taken in various circumstances). The nurse, as a moral agent for the patient, must be ready and able to advocate for the patient's rights and needs whenever necessary while providing care.</li>
<li>Assuming such a stance involves acting on ethical principles and values. Nurses must be prepared to identify advocacy issues and take action on them as needed. The nurse-patient relationship not only allows the nurse to support the patient, but it also supports the nurse.</li>
<li>Nurses can empower patients by providing opportunities for them to make autonomous decisions about their health care. They can support patient empowerment through education about appropriate administrative protocols (eg, patients' rights, hospital policies, procedures) that best meet individual patient's needs.</li>
<li>When dealing with informed consent, the nurse's role is to validate that the patient has been given the information and understands as much as is possible about the surgical intervention. The nurse's assessment includes determining whether the patient has any additional questions that might require another discussion with the physician. The nurse also assesses the level of decision making the patient is able to demonstrate.</li>
<li>The principle of autonomy provides for patients to make decisions freely, even if those decisions are against medical advice.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>37</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The criterion that must be met is that the patient is an adult who is capable of making decisions and has been given the information necessary to make an autonomous choice.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Even if a surgeon and nurse believe that surgery is in the best interest of the patient, the patient has the right to refuse the procedure at any time, regardless of whether he or she signed a surgical consent form.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nurses ethically should support patients in their choices, regardless of whether they agree with the patient's decision.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nursing assessment and care also applies to situations in which patients identify advance directive choices or decisions related to do-not-resuscitate orders.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is the nurse's role to ensure that surgical team members are aware of a patient's wishes in these matters. It is important that all team members and the patient discuss and identify a plan of care before beginning the surgical procedure.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="respect-for-others">Respect for others<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#respect-for-others" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Not only must nurses recognize the individuality of their patients, they also must recognize the individuality of their colleagues and others.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nurses must be able to interact with a variety of other professionals and ancillary providers in the perioperative environment. Treating others with professionalism and respect enhances the performance of the health care team.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nurses are obligated to treat all persons in a just and fair manner, regardless of disability or economic, educational, cultural, religious, racial, age, and lifestyle differences.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Just as nurses have the right not to be abused or harassed in the workplace, so must they treat others in the workplace with respect and compassion. The nurse recognizes the contributions of each member of the health care team and collaborates to achieve quality patient care.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ethical-dilemmas">Ethical dilemmas<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-dilemmas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>38</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nurses often are faced with an ethical dilemma when a patient is anxious because he or she does not understand fully what is going to happen in surgery and the nurse is being pressured for a fast turnover time.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse is faced with conflicting expectations (i.e., the patient's emotional needs, expectations to be efficient). Nurses following the ethical principles of compassion and respect would place a patient's emotional needs above expediting the surgical schedule.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In addition, there may be times when a perioperative nurse is told to get the patient's signature on a consent form. Nurses must realize that they are not being asked to provide informed consent for the patient. In cases such as these, the nurse merely is acting as a witness to the identity of the patient and to the patient's signature on the consent form.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If a nurse is present at the time the patient signs the consent, it is a good opportunity to once again assess the patient's level of understanding and see if he or she wishes to further discuss the proposed intervention with the physician.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treating-patients-equally">Treating patients equally<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treating-patients-equally" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nursing care should be provided in a non-prejudicial manner that preserves and protects patient free will, choice, and human rights.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When providing patient care, nurses must take into consideration a patient's values, religious beliefs, and lifestyle choices.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These choices and beliefs influence nursing practice to the extent that they represent factors the nurse must understand, consider, and respect in tailoring care to personal needs and maintaining an individual's self-respect and dignity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse does not have to agree with or condone the choices and beliefs of the patient, but he or she should not allow any such disagreement to preclude appropriate patient care.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>39</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nurses may need to plan for appropriate substitute nursing care if their personal beliefs conflict with required care; this respects the patient's health care decisions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The principle of <strong>justice</strong> dictates that all patients receive the same care regardless of personal attributes. A wealthy patient should receive the same perioperative care as a patient from a lower economic status.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Privacy and confidentiality</strong> are to be maintained too, regardless of the personal characteristics of the patient.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nurses apply ethical principles by using standards of nursing practice consistently to all patients regardless of disability or economic, educational, cultural, religious, racial, age, or lifestyle differences.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ethical perioperative nursing behavior also is demonstrated by refraining from making derogatory comments about patients, family members, significant others, colleagues, and other associates.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="age-specific-care">Age-specific care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#age-specific-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>As a part of respect for individuals, perioperative nurses must act ethically with regard to age-specific care and treatment. E.g sometimes it is difficult for nurses to adequately assess pain in patients. As a result, they subjectively decide what is best for the patient based on their depth of knowledge and individual assessment skills; thus, some nurses may be more aggressive than others when managing pain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nurses often use the principle of best interests, which allows them to act as most reasonable people would act in similar circumstances. This principle is used most often in cases in which patients cannot speak for themselves or cannot accurately relate their feelings to the nurse, such as in the case of pediatric patients.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It often is necessary to consult with a pediatric patient's parents when obtaining assessment data. A nurse acting with the best interests of the patient in mind must consider individual patient needs, parental preferences where applicable, and professional standards of practice. In essence, the good of pain management has to be</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>balanced with the potential for harm to minimize or eliminate any harm that may result.</p>
<ul>
<li>In this role, the nurse becomes the parental surrogate, advocating for the child, assessing pain, and providing timely and effective relief. Understanding pain management across the</li>
<li>life span, therefore, becomes an integral part of the ethical practice of nurses. With an understanding of the ethical principles and responsibilities inherent to nursing practice, perioperative nurses will be able to more effectively manage preoperative, intraoperative, and postoperative pain.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-changing-face-of-culture">The changing face of culture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-changing-face-of-culture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Perioperative nurses provide nursing care directed to meet the comprehensive needs of all patients, taking into consideration aspects of culture, language, perception of pain, significant others, values, and beliefs. As individuals, nurses bring assumptions from their own culture, as well as assumptions</li>
<li>about the cultures of others, to their practice. To provide care that is relevant culturally to a diverse patient population, it is vital that nurses recognize the importance of being aware of and sensitive to the values, beliefs, and health practices of different cultures.</li>
<li>Culturally competent care has been defined as a complex integration of knowledge, attitudes, and skill that enhances cross-cultural communication and appropriate and effective interaction with others. In many instances, nurses provide care across cultures, so it becomes an ethical imperative for them to develop culturally competent caring.</li>
<li>To effectively care for patients from other cultures, nurses must be conscientious observers and perceptive listeners and assessors. Acquiring information about a patient's culture and gaining further personal insight provides nurses with an increased understanding of culture and values as they relate to providing culturally competent care from both the patient's and the nurse's perspective.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Examples of this in perioperative practice occur when a nurse provides language interpreters for spiritual comfort and care, regardless of the patient's health status. Sometimes perioperative nurses can allow family members to be present at various times during the surgical experience to alleviate anxiety on the part of a patient from a different culture.</li>
<li>Sometimes all that is necessary is allowing a patient to bring an important cultural or religious item (eg, a talisman, rosary) into surgery. The item often can be put in a plastic bag so the patient still can have contact with it even as sterility is maintained in the operating room.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="case-study-1">CASE STUDY 1<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#case-study-1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A 44-year-old woman, is brought into the operation theatre for a vaginal hysterectomy. She speaks and understands english well and is in good health with no abnormal risks for the procedure.</p>
<p>In the preoperative area, she tells the circulating nurse that she is very shy and concerned about privacy issues, especially as related to her cultural beliefs. She would like as few people as possible in the operation room during her surgery. The nurse assures her that all efforts will be taken to ensure her privacy in surgery, but that there is a need for operation room team members to be present.</p>
<p>As this patient is transferring to the operation room bed, the surgeon walks in with his 14-year-old son, who is dressed appropriately for the surgical setting. The surgeon tells the patient that it is take-your- daughter/son-to-work week, and he has brought his son in to see her surgical procedure. He asks the patient if it would be all right if his son were scrubbed in at the field to observe her procedure. She stammers that she is uncertain about such observers. The surgeon replies that it is only his son and he will be no trouble as he will just stand by and watch. At this point, the patient appears unable to answer. She looks around the room and locks her gaze onto the nurse's eyes.</p>
<p>The nurse, in this situation, needs to identify the ethical issues involved. The issues involve patient autonomy, dignity, cultural beliefs and rights. To make an autonomous decision, a person must have true freedom to refuse. If this freedom is eliminated, then consent is meaningless. The patient in this case is being asked to consent to an additional observer in the</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>room. To ask a patient this immediately before she undergoes a procedure puts her in a position of duress or coercion. The patient may not feel that she has a true choice or the ability to refuse in such a situation.</p>
<p>The nurse must help the surgeon identify that the patient feels uncomfortable with the surgeon's son in the room and ask that he leaves. The patient on the other hand needs to feel that her decision not to have the surgeon's son in the operation room will not in any way prejudice her treatment from the surgeon or other members of the health care team. The team members need to understand that certain cultures may value privacy and that this is an aspect of human rights and dignity.</p>
<p>Additionally, the nurse must be aware of the element of risk that comes when any observer is allowed into the perioperative environment. It is imperative for the safety of the patient and the observer that any person coming into the operation room be trained appropriately in blood and body fluid precautions and contamination.</p>
<p>In this case, some potential risks could occur. First, the surgeon's son may contaminate the field and put the patient at risk and second, he may faint and injure himself or some else as he falls. Thirdly, he also may become contaminated with blood or body fluids during the procedure, because he is not trained in the proper protocols.</p>
<p>Most importantly, however, is the patient's right to refuse the observer. The patient should not be put in such a last minute consent situation. Patients may feel compromised, coerced, or violated by such a request.</p>
<p>Often patients are too worried about their procedures to even consider refusal as an option. They do not want their surgeons to get angry with them for saying no.</p>
<p>In this example, the perioperative nurse should take immediate action to postpone the anesthesia induction to explain the patient's concerns to the surgeon before proceeding. To avoid a confrontation in front of the patient, the perioperative nurse should speak with the surgeon privately.</p>
<p>The perioperative nurse and the surgeon then should reassure the patient that her wishes have been honored and her privacy will be maintained throughout the procedure.</p>
<p>Conclusion</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The strength of the ethical perspective is its prescriptive nature. It promotes an action guide for nurses to follow in the realm of patient care. Ethics, as a branch of philosophy, incorporates multiple approaches to take when dealing with or applying principles to real-life situations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Each perioperative nurse may experience a situation differently and also may address the situation and identify the ethical conflict issues and his or her feelings, behaviors, actions, analysis, and resolution of the situation differently.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health care delivery provided by a surgical team does not create ethical conflicts necessarily, but it may highlight conflicts if the values of team members emphasize different priorities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Additionally, new roles among health care team members may carry expectations about how members should interact with each other and how standards of care should be met.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perioperative nurses, by virtue of the nurse-patient relationship, have obligations to provide safe, professional, and ethical patient care.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is important that nurses know how to manage ethical decisions appropriately so patients' ethical rights can be honored without compromising the nurse's own moral conscience.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ethical practice, thus, is a critical aspect of nursing care and the development of ethical competency is paramount for present and future nursing practice.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="theatre-design-considerations">Theatre design considerations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theatre-design-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The design depends on the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>Number, type and length of the surgical procedure to be carried out.</li>
<li>Type and distribution of specialties of the surgical team and the equipment required by each.</li>
<li>Staff, patients and other personnel safety during construction and renovation.</li>
<li>Equipments and surgical specialty</li>
<li>Scheduling policy</li>
</ol>

<ol start="6">
<li>Volumes i.e. patients and size of the hospital.</li>
<li>Planned technology.</li>
<li>Future plans expansion.</li>
<li>Systems and procedures for efficient patient, staff and supplies flow</li>
<li>Scheduling policies related to the number of hours per day and days per week the suit will be in use.</li>
<li>Design, ventilation and control of pollution and traffic all need to be considered in the design of the operating room.</li>
<li>A proper design of the operating theatre allows a one way flow of traffic and prevents the return flow of contaminants in to the clean area.</li>
<li>Operated patient should not meet with the un-operated patient</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="theatre-light">Theatre light<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theatre-light" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="fluorescent-lighting">Fluorescent lighting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fluorescent-lighting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="size-of-theatre">Size of theatre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#size-of-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wall-and-ceiling">Wall and ceiling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wall-and-ceiling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Walls and ceilings should be solid without windows</li>
<li>Finishes of all surface material should be hard, non porous, fire resistant, waterproof, stain proof, seamless, non reflective and easy to clean.</li>
<li>The ceiling should be a minimum of 10 feet high and have seamless construction</li>
<li>The ceiling colour should be white to reflect at least 90% of the light in even dispersion.</li>
<li>Walls should be pastel colour (soft, neutral e.g. baby blue) with paneling made of hard vinyl materials that is easy to clean and maintain.</li>
<li>The walls should have stainless cuffs at collision corner to prevent damage.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="floors">Floors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#floors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The floor should be made of antistatic materials.</li>
<li>It should be probably made of terrazzo or seamless polyvinyl chloride that is continued up the sides of the wall for about six inches.</li>
<li>The material should not degrade or wear out with aging and cleaning.</li>
<li>They should be slip-proof when wet</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="doors-and-ventilation">Doors and ventilation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#doors-and-ventilation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Doors:</strong></li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Should be about 4ft wide</li>
<li>Sliding doors, that can be swung open when necessary</li>
<li>They should not remain open during surgical procedures</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><strong>Ventilation:</strong></li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Air movement and air conditioning in the operating theatre are regulated so that the patient and theatre staff are comfortable.</li>
<li>Air flow in the operating room is directed clean to less clean areas.</li>
<li>Relative humidity is maintained at between 50-55%</li>
<li>Heat and water loss can occur in small babies during prolonged operations in cool air conditioning, hence humidity needs to be adjusted</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="traffic-flow">Traffic flow<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#traffic-flow" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li><strong>Unrestricted area:</strong></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Personnel may wear street cloths, and traffic is not limited.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li><strong>In semi-restricted area:</strong></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Such as processing and storage areas for instruments and supplies, as well as corridors leading to the restricted areas of the surgical suite, personnel must wear surgical attire and patients must wear gowns and hair coverings</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li><strong>Restricted area:</strong></li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>This includes operating room and clean core and scrub sink areas.</li>
<li>Surgical attire and mask are required in these areas when there are open sterile supplies or scrubbed persons in the area.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>The flow of supplies should be from clean core area through the operating rooms to the peripheral corridor.</li>
<li>Soiled materials should not re-enter the clean core area</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="traffic-patterns">Traffic patterns<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#traffic-patterns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the restricted areas there are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Open sterile supplies</li>
<li>Scrubbed personnel</li>
<li>All personnel should wear masks and caps</li>
<li>Sterile procedures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="semi-restricted-area">Semi restricted area:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#semi-restricted-area" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Personnel to wear scrubs/theatre attire, and caps</li>
<li>Patients hair should be covered</li>
<li>Only authorized personnel</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="location">Location<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#location" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Critical Care Unit</li>
<li>Sterile Supplies Area</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-general-instruments">Basic general instruments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-general-instruments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
