<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintaining-a-sterile-field-principles-of-aseptic-technique">Maintaining a sterile field/Principles of aseptic technique<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintaining-a-sterile-field-principles-of-aseptic-technique" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Placing sterile items within sterile field and only sterile items are used within sterile field</li>
<li>Opening, dispensing or transferring sterile items without contaminating them.</li>
<li>Not allowing sterile personnel to reach across unsterile areas and touch unsterile items</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
51
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Not allowing unsterile personnel to reach across the sterile field or to touch sterile items.</li>
<li>Whatever is sterile for one patient can only be used for that patient.</li>
<li>You must pour sterile fluids from a point high enough to prevent accidental touching of the receptacle, but this should not produce splashing.</li>
<li>If there is any doubt about the sterility of an article or area, it is considered unsterile</li>
<li>Sterile objects become unsterile when touched by unsterile objects.</li>
<li>Sterile items that are out of vision or below the waist level of the nurse are considered unsterile.</li>
<li>Sterile objects can become unsterile by prolong exposure to airborne microorganisms.</li>
<li>The edges of a sterile field are considered unsterile.</li>
<li>Gowns of the surgical team are considered sterile in front from the chest to the level of the sterile field. The sleeves are also considered sterile from 2 inches above the elbow to the stockinette cup.</li>
<li>Sterile drapes are used to create a sterile field. Only the top surface of a draped table is considered sterile. During draping of a table or patient, the sterile drape is held well above the surface to be covered and is positioned from front to back.</li>
<li>A tear or puncture of the drape permitting access to an unsterile surface underneath renders the area unsterile. Such a drape must be replaced.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="safety-and-infection-prevention-in-theatre">Safety and infection prevention in theatre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safety-and-infection-prevention-in-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Safety and infection prevention are of utmost importance in the operating theatre. To ensure this, some of the things considered are the following :</p>
<ul>
<li>Preparation of the operating theatre</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Theatre nurse</li>
<li>Patient and equipment</li>
<li>The equipment used in theatre and types of anaesthesia</li>
<li>Operating room</li>
<li>Setting sterile trolley</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation-of-the-operating-room">Preparation of the operating room<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-the-operating-room" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The theatre and equipment must be cleaned thoroughly every morning to minimise the number of micro-organisms.</li>
<li>Ensure high dusting of walls and clean trolleys, drip stand, operating tables and all equipment there in.</li>
<li>You should also ensure that the floor is scrubbed with soapy water to remove dirt and then mopped with a disinfectant recommended by the hospital.</li>
<li>After cleaning and drying the theatre floor, all the equipment must be returned to its proper place and ensure they are working.</li>
<li>Prepare the operating table by drying it after cleaning and placing it in the right position directly below the overhead operating lights. Theatre table should then be draped with a clean sheet ready to receive the patient.</li>
<li>You should then set the anaesthetic tray ready</li>
<li>Check the diathermy machine to ensure it is in working order for use to cauterise any bleeding vessel during operation.</li>
<li>The operating lights should be checked to ensure they are in good working order.</li>
<li>The required operating set of equipment should be ordered from the theatre sterilising room/unit.</li>
<li>After the operation has been completed you should:</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>53</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Clean all fitments and equipment thoroughly</li>
<li>Do high and low level dusting using the disinfectant</li>
<li>Clean the floor and drains with the disinfectant</li>
<li>Wipe the operating lights with a clean damp towel</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation-of-the-nurse">Preparation of the Nurse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-the-nurse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>After entering the theatre unit, you should go straight to the changing rooms.</li>
<li>Take a shower and change into your theatre suit and boots. Personal clothes should be locked in a locker within the changing room.</li>
<li>Your head should be covered with a clean, sterile theatre cap.</li>
<li>If you have any respiratory infection you are advised not to enter the operating room.</li>
<li>A very high standard of personal hygiene should be maintained.</li>
<li>You should avoid movement in and out of the theatre and any time that happens you should change into another clean theatre suit before re-entering the operating room.</li>
<li>It is advisable for you to visit the toilet to empty your bowels and bladder before taking a shower and putting on the sterile theatre suit to minimise the need of using this facility later during the theatre activities.</li>
<li>However, this is just a precautionary measure and you should change your theatre suit any time the toilet facilities are used if you are to go back to the operating room.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="scrubbing">Scrubbing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scrubbing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is done to remove micro-organisms from the forearm and arms by mechanical washing and chemical disinfections before taking part in surgical procedure.</li>
<li>This helps prevent the possibility of the patient being contaminated by bacteria from the hands and arms.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Preparation for this procedure involves the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>The theatre suit should have the top/shirt tidily tucked in. Roll the sleeves up to at least three inches above the elbow.</li>
<li>A cap should be worn to cover all the hair, tie the tape at the back.</li>
<li>A mask should be worn with the short side above the nose and the long side under the chin.</li>
<li>Remove all jewellery, wedding rings, dress rings, watches, earrings and necklaces.</li>
<li>Finger nails must be short and clean without nail varnish.</li>
<li>No cut wounds or septic wound on fingers. No upper respiratory tract infection.</li>
<li>No gastroenteritis.</li>
<li>Wear a mackintosh apron to protect your scrub suit. Regulate temperature and flow of water to suit you.</li>
<li>Scrubbing time varies according to the type of soap or chemical used.</li>
<li>E.G if using gamophen soap, which contains hexachlorophene disinfectants, you should scrub for five minutes; if using hibiscrub, two minutes; ordinary soap, ten to fifteen minutes.</li>
</ol>
<p>For the procedure refer to the nursing council procedure manual</p>
<p>Drying / gowning and gloving</p>
<ol>
<li>Drying :</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Pick up the towel and step back.</li>
<li>Start with the left hand and blot dry the fingers, the webs of the hand and the palm well, then move to the back of the hand, and the forearm, using a circular movement to the elbows.</li>
<li>Change the towel to the left hand with the wet part against the left palm. Using the dry part of the towel, repeat the same procedure on the other arm.</li>
<li>When you get to the elbow, discard the used towel in the dispenser provided.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Gowning</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on
55
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The following procedure should be followed when gowning:</p>
<ol>
<li>Pick a gown and step back.</li>
<li>Hold the neck-band and let the bottom hem drop.</li>
<li>Open the gown and slide both hands in through the arm holes.</li>
<li>Do not touch the outside of the gown with your bare hands.</li>
<li>The Runner Nurse will first tie the neck and shoulder bands then wastbands without touching the gown.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-gloving">3. Gloving<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-gloving" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedure should be adhered to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Arrange gloves on the trolley with glove finger portion away from you.</li>
<li>Pick the glove with left hand holding at the folded part and slip in your right hand. Fold the tip of the sleeve on right hand and pass the glove over.</li>
<li>Using the gloved hand slip your fingers beneath the folded area of the remaining glove and slip in the left hand into the glove.</li>
<li>Unroll the cuff of the glove covering the cuff of the sleeve.</li>
<li>Do the same for the opposite hand using the same technique.</li>
<li>Ensure you do not contaminate any area that will come in contact with the sterile field.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="patients-preparation">Patients preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patients-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Skin preparation depends on the area being operated.</li>
<li>Preparation of the skin includes vigorous sponging of the skin with a sponge soaked in strong disinfectant held in a sponge holding forceps.</li>
<li>Disinfectants used include centrimide and hibitine in spirit. After sponging, the area is swabbed once with iodine in spirit or hibitine 5% in 70% alcohol.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="after-skin-preparation-the-patient-is-draped">After skin preparation the patient is draped:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#after-skin-preparation-the-patient-is-draped" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The purpose of draping is to maintain an adequate sterile field for the surgical procedure.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The scrub nurse gives the surgeon the sterile towel to cover the area above the operation site and below and the sides.</p>
<p>After draping, the scrub nurse brings the operation trolley and instrument trolley next to the table.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="setting-up-a-sterile-trolley">Setting up a Sterile Trolley<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#setting-up-a-sterile-trolley" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Done by a theatre nurse after scrubbing, putting on the required operating room attire</li>
<li>The runner nurse/circulating nurse assists the scrub nurse in setting up the trolley e.g. opening the green towels drum, sterile gloves</li>
<li>Several trolleys and packs are required while setting the trolleys for specific operations</li>
<li>Instruments, , drapes , extra instruments are arranged according to the order of use</li>
<li>Counts must be maintained</li>
<li>When the trolley is fully set it should be covered with sterile towel till the operation starts</li>
<li>Extra materials e.g. consumables may be added according to the need by the circulating nurse</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="positioning-patient-in-theatre">Positioning patient in Theatre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positioning-patient-in-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Positioning is done by the other team members who have not scrubbed up and worn sterile gowns and gloves.</li>
<li>Patients are positioned before the skin preparation and draping described previously.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="goals-of-proper-positioning">Goals of proper positioning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goals-of-proper-positioning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>To maintain patients airway and avoid constriction or pressure on the chest cavity</li>
<li>To maintain circulation</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>57</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>To prevent nerve damage</li>
<li>To prevent bed sores</li>
<li>To provide comfort and safety to the patient during the operation.</li>
<li>To allow the procedure to be done on the patient</li>
</ol>
<p>NB: The nurse must be aware of the anatomic and physiological changes associated with patient positioning, and any procedure being done.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="positions-used-in-surgery">Positions used in surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positions-used-in-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-trendelenburg-position">1. trendelenburg position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-trendelenburg-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Trendelenburg, which is most commonly used in pelvic operations, where the patient is placed supine while the table is modified to a head tilt of 30-45 degrees and the table is broken at the knee joint to lower the lower section slightly to flex the patient's knees.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251229-5f1732e2.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-reverse-trendelenburg">2. Reverse trendelenburg<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-reverse-trendelenburg" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The entire bed is tilted so the head is higher than the feet.</li>
<li>Used for head and neck procedures.</li>
<li>Facilitates exposure, aids in breathing and decrease blood supply to the area.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kidney-position">Kidney position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kidney-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Kidney position, where the bridge of the table is raised to elevate the loins between the lower limbs and the iliac crest.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251229-5cb1acf6.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lithotomy">Lithotomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lithotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Lithotomy, which is used in perineum operation. The patient lies supine position and the lower limbs are raised and abducted to expose perineum, the legs and feet are on stirrups that support the lower extremities, they should at even height. Both legs must be raised simultaneously to avoid injury. The knees are flexed.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251229-d79655d6.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="supine-or-laparotomy-position">Supine or laparotomy position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supine-or-laparotomy-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Supine (laparotomy position), where the patient lies on the back spinal column should be in a alignment with the legs parallel to the bed, head in line with spin and face is upward, with arms on the sides on arm boards.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251229-aad6c681.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prone-position">Prone position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prone-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Anesthetized supine, usually on the stretcher prior to turning, Face down, resting on the abdomen and chest, Head is turned to one side with accessible airway, Forehead, eyes and chin are protected Access to the posterior fossa of the skull, the posterior spine, the buttocks and perirectal area, and the lower extremities</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="laminectomy-position">Laminectomy Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laminectomy-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Laminectomy position, where the patient is put in the prone position with the head beyond the end of the table with the forehead resting and supported on a horseshoe fixed six inches below the level of the table.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251229-13be1397.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sutures-and-ligature">Sutures and Ligature<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sutures-and-ligature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A suture is a medical device used to hold skin, internal organs, blood vessels or other tissues of a human body together after they have been severed by injury or surgery until healing takes place.</li>
<li>A ligature is a suture used for tying blood vessels to a or another hollow organ to shut it off.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-sutures">Classification of sutures:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-sutures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Absorbable they are broken down in the tissue after some time</li>
<li>Non Absorbable the body tissues cannot digest the material used thus they are removable.</li>
</ol>
<p>The above suture can further be classified as :</p>
<ul>
<li>Natural or synthetic</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
61
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Monofilament or multifilament</li>
<li>Multi-stranded</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="natural-absorbable-suture-e-g-catgut">Natural absorbable suture e.g. catgut<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#natural-absorbable-suture-e-g-catgut" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Natural absorbable suture are defined by the loss of most of their tensile strength within 60 days after placement</li>
<li>They are of materials that are degraded by the body tissues</li>
<li>Originally they were made from sheeps intestines</li>
<li>Gut sutures are made of specially prepared beef and gut intestines and packaged in alcohol to prevent it from dying and breaking</li>
<li>It is multifilament</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examples">Examples:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examples" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Plain catgut  untreated</li>
<li>Chromic catgut turned with chromium salts to increase their persistent in the body</li>
<li>Chromic catgut tensile strength 10-21 days</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="synthetic-absorbable-suture">Synthetic absorbable suture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#synthetic-absorbable-suture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="examples-are">Examples are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examples-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Polyglycolic acid (DEXON) synthetic multifilament</li>
<li>Polyglatin (VICRYL) synthetic multifilament</li>
<li>Polydioxanone</li>
<li>Poliglecaprone Monocryl</li>
<li>Polyconate (MAXOM)</li>
</ol>
<p>62</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Poly trimethylene carbonate suture synthetic monofilament</li>
</ol>
<p>NB: Advantage to catgut is that it takes longer time in tissues than chromic catgut</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="non-absorbable-sutures">Non absorbable sutures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-absorbable-sutures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>They are resistant to degradation by living tissue, i.e they are not affected by the biological activities of the body tissues hence permanent unless removed</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Skin or wound closure where the sutures can be removed after a period</li>
<li>Can be used In inner tissues in which absorbable sutures are not adequate e.g. heart and blood vessels who rhythmic movements requires a suture which stays longer than three weeks to give wound enough time to heal</li>
</ol>
<p>NB: Non absorbable sutures can be permanently implanted in the body or can be removed after few days of surgery depending on the kind of surgery</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-natural-non-absorbable-sutures">1. Natural non absorbable sutures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-natural-non-absorbable-sutures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>a) Stainless steel
b) Silk
c) Cotton
d) Linen</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-synthetic-non-absorbable-sutures">2. Synthetic non absorbable sutures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-synthetic-non-absorbable-sutures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>&gt; Synthetic monofilament sutures are commonly used in cutaneous procedures and include</p>
<ol>
<li>Nylon</li>
<li>Polypropylene</li>
<li>Polyester</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-sutures">Characteristics of sutures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-sutures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>63</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Main characteristics to be considered in the selection of suture material :</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Tensile strength</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Elasticity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Plasticity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>memory</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ease of passage through tissue</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Knot security</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pull of tissue by suture</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Short and long term reactions of tissue</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Handling, ease of use of suture and packing property ensuring suture getting out of package with minimum memory.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Elasticity:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>It is a term describing elongation of suture material by means of pulling method then returning to its original length when left free, in short its flexibility.</li>
<li>Elasticity is a preferred characteristic sutures. Because after implanting the suture to the wound, suture is expected to keep two parts of scar together in suitable position by elongating without stressing, cutting tissues due to edema developed in the scar and then, upon retraction of wound after re-absorption of edema to return to original length.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Plasticity:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Plasticity is a term defined as the capacity of a suture to retain its length and strength after stretching.</li>
<li>Sutures with high plasticity do not hinder circulation on the tissue by elongating without stressing or cutting tissues due to developing edema on the wound.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>However, elongated suture upon retraction of wound after re-absorption of edema cannot ensure correct approximation of wound edges.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-memory">3. Memory:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-memory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is a term defining <strong>incapability of suture to change shape easily</strong>. Sutures with strong memory tend to return their former, packing form when they are removed from their packing, during and after manipulation. This is because of their rigidity.</li>
<li>Sutures with strong memory is hard to manipulate and thread, at the same time they have poor thread safety.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-friction-surface">4. Friction Surface:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-friction-surface" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It defines slipperiness of suture. Suture surface should be smooth and uniform. However, very slippery and smooth sutures are not preferred due to their unsecure knotting.</li>
<li>Uneven surface of sutures is a desired characteristic for knot security.</li>
<li>Disadvantages of these types of sutures (uneven sutures) are their leading trauma while passing through tissue and to thrombosis by scratching vein surface. Such disadvantages are tried to be eliminated by coating such sutures with materials such as silicone.</li>
<li>Multifilament sutures have larger friction surfaces compared to monofilament sutures and they cause more trauma while passing through tissues.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-tensile-strength">5. Tensile Strength:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-tensile-strength" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It defines the force needed to break the suture. Tensile strength of suture reduces after implantation.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>65</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Tensile strength is related with the diameter of suture and tensile strength increases as the diameter of suture increases.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weakest point of suture is knot. Therefore tensile strength of sutures are measured in knotted condition. Knotted suture has 2/3 strength of unknotted suture. Each applied knot reduces tensile strength of suture by 30-40% and causes to leave more foreign substance on the tissue.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol start="6">
<li>Capillarity:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It defines wicking of fluids by the suture and transmission of fluid wicked throughout the suture.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sutures with capillarity property carry the serum and bacteria in the region of implantation they have absorbed throughout the suture. Generally, capillarity of multifilament sutures are higher than monofilament ones.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sutures with capillary characteristic used on skin allow passage of microorganisms between external medium and internal medium and lead contamination.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Capillarity characteristics of sutures are minimized by coating with materials such as silicone, Teflon or resin.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol start="7">
<li>Pliability:</li>
</ol>
<p>This refers to the ease of handling suture material. So it is the ability to adjust knot tension and secure knots (related to suture material, filament types and diameter)</p>
<p>Factors impacting suture selection</p>
<ol>
<li>Field of specialism</li>
<li>Clinical tissue regeneration experiences</li>
<li>Surgery experience</li>
<li>Knowledge gained on healing process of tissue</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Knowledge on biological and physical characteristics of various suture materials</li>
<li>Patient factors (age, weight, general health status, existence of infection)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="usage-characteristics">Usage characteristics:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#usage-characteristics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It defines usage quality comprehensively. It includes all physical characteristics of suture such as handling, knot security, friction coefficient and memory.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="suture-sizes">Suture sizes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#suture-sizes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Suture sizes are classified according to USA Pharmacopoeia (USP) and European Pharmacopoeia (EP) which is also called as metric system.</li>
<li>Suture sizes commonly classified according to USP. USP classification is made according to diameter, tensile strength and knot security of the suture.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; 12/0  7/0 = Microsurgery (smallest in diameter, weaker)
&gt; 6/0 = Face and Blood Vessels
&gt; 5/0 = Face, neck and blood vessels
&gt; 4/0 = Mucosa, neck, hands, arms, legs, tendon, blood vessels,
&gt; 3/0 = arm, legs, body, intestine, blood vessel,
&gt; 2/0 = Body, fascia, stomach, internal organs, blood vessel
&gt; 0-1 = Abdominal wall, strong fascia surfaces. (largest in diameter, Strongest)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-needle">Surgical needle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-needle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Needles are necessary for placement of suture material in the wound.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
67
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>They should be:</p>
<ol>
<li>Made of high quality stainless steel</li>
<li>As slim as possible without compromising strength</li>
<li>Sharp enough to penetrate tissue with no trauma</li>
<li>Be rigid enough to resist bending</li>
<li>Malleable (flexible) enough to bend before breaking.</li>
</ol>
<p>Sterile and corrosion resistant to prevent introduction of microorganism or foreign bodies into the wound</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="needle-construction">Needle construction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#needle-construction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The needle has 3 sections:</p>
<ul>
<li>The point: this is the sharpest portion and used to penetrate the tissue.</li>
<li>The body: this represents the mid portion of the needle.</li>
<li>The swage: this is the thickest portion of the needle and the portion to which the suture material is attached</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-needles">Types of needles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-needles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Round bodied needles, which are round and smooth, cause less damage and make a puncture. They are used in delicate tissues and organs e.g. uterus, intestines, (all the internal organs)</li>
<li>Atraumatic needles, which are either cutting or round bodied whose traumatising chance is minimal. These needles have no eye. Suture and needles are made joined-together.</li>
<li>Cutting needles, which have a sharp edge, cut a crack as they pass, and are used on strong tissues, for example, skin, tendon, muscles.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="swabs">Swabs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#swabs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Swabs are resources/any porous material used in an open wound during surgery for absorbing blood and fluids, protecting tissues, applying pressure or traction and dissecting tissue during a surgical intervention.</li>
<li>A radio-opaque thread or marker is incorporated into commercially manufactured swabs.</li>
<li>There are different types of swabs:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Gauze swabs 3" X 3" (7.6 x 7.6) cm which are used for small. incisions;</li>
<li>4" x 4" (10 x 10) cm; raytec swabs or dissecting swabs.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-type-of-swabs-are">Other type of swabs are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-type-of-swabs-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol start="3">
<li>Large abdominal swabs; with attached tapes</li>
<li>Small abdominal swabs; usually used in the bladder</li>
<li>Peanut swabs or lahey swabs; small round gauze sponges used for blunt dissections or to absorb fluid in delicate procedures e.g. thyroidectomy</li>
<li>Large and small tonsil swabs which are cotton filled gauze with cotton thread attached.</li>
<li>Neuro - patties made of compressed rayon of cotton, used moist on delicate structures such as the brain or spinal cord</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="care-of-swabs-instruments-and-needles">Care of swabs, instruments and needles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-swabs-instruments-and-needles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="prior-to-sterilization">Prior to Sterilization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prior-to-sterilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Use clean, uncontaminated, new swabs.</li>
<li>Check all swabs and shake well before folding and packing; no wool, threads or pieces of lint should adhere to the swab.</li>
<li>Swabs must be X-Ray opaque and abdominal swabs must have 25cm tapes.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
69
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The first and second checker must do a simultaneous check.</li>
<li>Each bundle must contain five swabs, abdominal, raytec and tonsil swabs are kept together with tape or a rubber band.</li>
<li>Point balls are sewn together and each bundle must contain a signed document.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="before-the-operation">Before the operation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#before-the-operation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The scrub nurse holds the bundle up and checks that each swab has a</p>
<ul>
<li>Secured tape and a opaque indicator.</li>
<li>He/she checks each swab separately into a bowl while counting audibly and must not count one bundle on top of another.</li>
<li>The scrub nurse must count audibly with the circulating nurse.</li>
</ul>
<p>If extra swabs are required during the operation, the same procedure is to be followed with number added on, e.g. <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>5</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>5</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>5</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">5 + 5 + 5</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span></span></span></span></span> or according to hospital policy</p>
<ul>
<li>Small dissecting swabs (laheys) are counted by holding one secure between fingers, counting that one and then pointing with the finger to the remaining four which are then placed in a gallipot.</li>
<li>Ensure that each has an X-Ray opaque indicator.</li>
<li>If any bundle of swabs opened is found to be incorrect, the swabs and document must be removed from the theatre to prevent later confusion.</li>
<li>The incorrect swabs must be given to the unit manager who must follow up this occurrence.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>No opened swabs are to be allowed in theatre if they are not counted. Swabs may not be used for cleaning theatres.</li>
<li>Before closure of the cavity, an audible check is done of the remaining swabs on the rack and those in use on the trolley and operating field.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rules-for-counting-swabs-intra-operative">Rules for counting swabs intra-operative<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rules-for-counting-swabs-intra-operative" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The rules for counting swabs in theatre is according to the scrub nurse's specific preference, complying with at least the following:</li>
<li>There should be a minimum of three (3) counts of swabs, though this is not fixed. If the scrub nurse is doing a long difficult procedure using many swabs she can do five to six counts.</li>
<li>It is up to the individual but the first swab count must be done before:</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; The peritoneum is closed, the next count is done before fascia is closed and the last count before the skin is sutured.</p>
<ul>
<li>Lahey swabs are not removed from the trolley, but checked into a gallipot / receiver.</li>
<li>It is important that the correct swab count is reported to the surgeon who must acknowledge this.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure-for-lost-swabs">Procedure for lost swabs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-for-lost-swabs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If the count is incorrect, inform the surgeon and do a recount.</li>
<li>The missing item must be looked for in the surgical cavity as well as in the theatre.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>In the event of the missing article not being found, the scrub nurse must inform the registered nurse in charge. X-Rays, must be taken and if the article is seen, the surgeon must re-open the cavity.</li>
<li>If no article shows on X-Ray the surgeon records on the patient's file stating the missing article does not show on X-Ray.</li>
<li>The scrub nurse will endorse the facts about missing items in red on the operative form and in the operation register.</li>
<li>The scrub nurse and check (circulating) nurse must write a statement and hand it to the nurse in charge.</li>
<li>The original statements are photo copied to distribute to the following significant supervisors; Chief Nursing Service Manager, Clinical Manager, Theatre Nursing Service Manager, Scrub Nurse and Floor Nurse.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>NB:</strong></p>
<p><strong>Surgical count/ Swab count policy:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Surgical count is the manual process to count the materials used in the sterile field to prevent retained surgical items in patients during surgery</li>
<li>The overriding principle for the count is that all swabs, instruments and needles MUST be accounted for at ALL times during an invasive surgical procedure or vaginal birth to prevent foreign body retention and subsequent injury to the patient.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Role of nurses in the operating room</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Receiving area nurse</li>
<li>Scrub nurse</li>
<li>Anesthetic nurse</li>
<li>Circulating nurse</li>
</ol>

<li>Role of the PACU (post anaesthetic unit) nurse</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-a-scrub-nurse">Role of a scrub nurse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-a-scrub-nurse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="checking-the-operating-light">Checking the operating light<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#checking-the-operating-light" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Maintains the sterile field and anticipates the needs of the surgical team.</li>
<li>Maintain count of items used in the sterile field</li>
<li>Communicates with the surgical team members on the condition of the patient.</li>
<li>Receives specimen from the surgeon and hands them over to the circulating nurse.</li>
<li>Assists during the closure of the incision.</li>
